different content. A server [MAY]{.bcp14} abort the connection if it
detects that the client reset the packet
number.[¶](#section-17.2.5.3-4){.pilcrow}

The connection IDs used in Initial and Retry packets exchanged between
client and server are copied to the transport parameters and validated
as described in [Section
7.3](#cid-auth){.xref}.[¶](#section-17.2.5.3-5){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
:::
:::
:::
:::

::: {#short-header}
::: {#section-17.3 .section}
### [17.3.](#section-17.3){.section-number .selfRef} [Short Header Packets](#name-short-header-packets){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-short-header-packets}

This version of QUIC defines a single packet type that uses the short
packet header.[¶](#section-17.3-1){.pilcrow}

::: {#packet-1rtt}
::: {#section-17.3.1 .section}
#### [17.3.1.](#section-17.3.1){.section-number .selfRef} [1-RTT Packet](#name-1-rtt-packet){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-1-rtt-packet}

A 1-RTT packet uses a short packet header. It is used after the version
and 1-RTT keys are negotiated.[¶](#section-17.3.1-1){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-1-rtt-packet-2}

::: {#section-17.3.1-2.1 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
    1-RTT Packet {
      Header Form (1) = 0,
      Fixed Bit (1) = 1,
      Spin Bit (1),
      Reserved Bits (2),
      Key Phase (1),
      Packet Number Length (2),
      Destination Connection ID (0..160),
      Packet Number (8..32),
      Packet Payload (8..),
    }
:::

[Figure 19](#figure-19){.selfRef}: [1-RTT
Packet](#name-1-rtt-packet-2){.selfRef}

1-RTT packets contain the following
fields:[¶](#section-17.3.1-3){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Header Form:

:   The most significant bit (0x80) of byte 0 is set to 0 for the short
    header.[¶](#section-17.3.1-4.2.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Fixed Bit:

:   The next bit (0x40) of byte 0 is set to 1. Packets containing a zero
    value for this bit are not valid packets in this version and
    [MUST]{.bcp14} be discarded. A value of 1 for this bit allows QUIC
    to coexist with other protocols; see
    \[[RFC7983](#RFC7983){.xref}\].[¶](#section-17.3.1-4.4.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Spin Bit:

:   The third most significant bit (0x20) of byte 0 is the latency spin
    bit, set as described in [Section
    17.4](#spin-bit){.xref}.[¶](#section-17.3.1-4.6.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Reserved Bits:

:   The next two bits (those with a mask of 0x18) of byte 0 are
    reserved. These bits are protected using header protection; see
    [Section
    5.4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9001#section-5.4){.relref} of
    \[[QUIC-TLS](#QUIC-TLS){.xref}\]. The value included prior to
    protection [MUST]{.bcp14} be set to 0. An endpoint [MUST]{.bcp14}
    treat receipt of a packet that has a non-zero value for these bits,
    after removing both packet and header protection, as a connection
    error of type PROTOCOL_VIOLATION. Discarding such a packet after
    only removing header protection can expose the endpoint to attacks;
    see [Section
    9.5](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9001#section-9.5){.relref} of
    \[[QUIC-TLS](#QUIC-TLS){.xref}\].[¶](#section-17.3.1-4.8.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Key Phase:

:   The next bit (0x04) of byte 0 indicates the key phase, which allows
    a recipient of a packet to identify the packet protection keys that
    are used to protect the packet. See \[[QUIC-TLS](#QUIC-TLS){.xref}\]
    for details. This bit is protected using header protection; see
    [Section
    5.4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9001#section-5.4){.relref} of
    \[[QUIC-TLS](#QUIC-TLS){.xref}\].[¶](#section-17.3.1-4.10.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Packet Number Length:

:   The least significant two bits (those with a mask of 0x03) of byte 0
    contain the length of the Packet Number field, encoded as an
    unsigned two-bit integer that is one less than the length of the
    Packet Number field in bytes. That is, the length of the Packet
    Number field is the value of this field plus one. These bits are
    protected using header protection; see [Section
    5.4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9001#section-5.4){.relref} of
    \[[QUIC-TLS](#QUIC-TLS){.xref}\].[¶](#section-17.3.1-4.12.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Destination Connection ID:

:   The Destination Connection ID is a connection ID that is chosen by
    the intended recipient of the packet. See [Section
    5.1](#connection-id){.xref} for more
    details.[¶](#section-17.3.1-4.14.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Packet Number:

:   The Packet Number field is 1 to 4 bytes long. The packet number is
    protected using header protection; see [Section
    5.4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9001#section-5.4){.relref} of
    \[[QUIC-TLS](#QUIC-TLS){.xref}\]. The length of the Packet Number
    field is encoded in Packet Number Length field. See [Section
    17.1](#packet-encoding){.xref} for
    details.[¶](#section-17.3.1-4.16.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Packet Payload:

:   1-RTT packets always include a 1-RTT protected
    payload.[¶](#section-17.3.1-4.18.1){.pilcrow}

:   

The header form bit and the Destination Connection ID field of a short
header packet are version independent. The remaining fields are specific
to the selected QUIC version. See
\[[QUIC-INVARIANTS](#QUIC-INVARIANTS){.xref}\] for details on how
packets from different versions of QUIC are
interpreted.[¶](#section-17.3.1-5){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
:::
:::

::: {#spin-bit}
::: {#section-17.4 .section}
### [17.4.](#section-17.4){.section-number .selfRef} [Latency Spin Bit](#name-latency-spin-bit){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-latency-spin-bit}

The latency spin bit, which is defined for 1-RTT packets ([Section
17.3.1](#packet-1rtt){.xref}), enables passive latency monitoring from
observation points on the network path throughout the duration of a
connection. The server reflects the spin value received, while the
client \"spins\" it after one RTT. On-path observers can measure the
time between two spin bit toggle events to estimate the end-to-end RTT
of a connection.[¶](#section-17.4-1){.pilcrow}

The spin bit is only present in 1-RTT packets, since it is possible to
measure the initial RTT of a connection by observing the handshake.
Therefore, the spin bit is available after version negotiation and
connection establishment are completed. On-path measurement and use of
the latency spin bit are further discussed in
\[[QUIC-MANAGEABILITY](#QUIC-MANAGEABILITY){.xref}\].[¶](#section-17.4-2){.pilcrow}

The spin bit is an [OPTIONAL]{.bcp14} feature of this version of QUIC.
An endpoint that does not support this feature [MUST]{.bcp14} disable
it, as defined below.[¶](#section-17.4-3){.pilcrow}

Each endpoint unilaterally decides if the spin bit is enabled or
disabled for a connection. Implementations [MUST]{.bcp14} allow
administrators of clients and servers to disable the spin bit either
globally or on a per-connection basis. Even when the spin bit is not
disabled by the administrator, endpoints [MUST]{.bcp14} disable their
use of the spin bit for a random selection of at least one in every 16
network paths, or for one in every 16 connection IDs, in order to ensure
that QUIC connections that disable the spin bit are commonly observed on
the network. As each endpoint disables the spin bit independently, this
ensures that the spin bit signal is disabled on approximately one in
eight network paths.[¶](#section-17.4-4){.pilcrow}

When the spin bit is disabled, endpoints [MAY]{.bcp14} set the spin bit
to any value and [MUST]{.bcp14} ignore any incoming value. It is
[RECOMMENDED]{.bcp14} that endpoints set the spin bit to a random value
either chosen independently for each packet or chosen independently for
each connection ID.[¶](#section-17.4-5){.pilcrow}

If the spin bit is enabled for the connection, the endpoint maintains a
spin value for each network path and sets the spin bit in the packet
header to the currently stored value when a 1-RTT packet is sent on that
path. The spin value is initialized to 0 in the endpoint for each
network path. Each endpoint also remembers the highest packet number
seen from its peer on each path.[¶](#section-17.4-6){.pilcrow}

When a server receives a 1-RTT packet that increases the highest packet
number seen by the server from the client on a given network path, it
sets the spin value for that path to be equal to the spin bit in the
received packet.[¶](#section-17.4-7){.pilcrow}

When a client receives a 1-RTT packet that increases the highest packet
number seen by the client from the server on a given network path, it
sets the spin value for that path to the inverse of the spin bit in the
received packet.[¶](#section-17.4-8){.pilcrow}

An endpoint resets the spin value for a network path to 0 when changing
the connection ID being used on that network
path.[¶](#section-17.4-9){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
:::
:::

::: {#transport-parameter-encoding}
::: {#section-18 .section}
## [18.](#section-18){.section-number .selfRef} [Transport Parameter Encoding](#name-transport-parameter-encodin){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-transport-parameter-encodin}

The extension_data field of the quic_transport_parameters extension
defined in \[[QUIC-TLS](#QUIC-TLS){.xref}\] contains the QUIC transport
parameters. They are encoded as a sequence of transport parameters, as
shown in [Figure
20](#transport-parameter-sequence){.xref}:[¶](#section-18-1){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-sequence-of-transport-param}

::: {#transport-parameter-sequence}
::: {#section-18-2.1 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
    Transport Parameters {
      Transport Parameter (..) ...,
    }
:::

[Figure 20](#figure-20){.selfRef}: [Sequence of Transport
Parameters](#name-sequence-of-transport-param){.selfRef}
:::

Each transport parameter is encoded as an (identifier, length, value)
tuple, as shown in [Figure
21](#transport-parameter-encoding-fig){.xref}:[¶](#section-18-3){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-transport-parameter-encoding}

::: {#transport-parameter-encoding-fig}
::: {#section-18-4.1 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
    Transport Parameter {
      Transport Parameter ID (i),
      Transport Parameter Length (i),
      Transport Parameter Value (..),
    }
:::

[Figure 21](#figure-21){.selfRef}: [Transport Parameter
Encoding](#name-transport-parameter-encoding){.selfRef}
:::

The Transport Parameter Length field contains the length of the
Transport Parameter Value field in bytes.[¶](#section-18-5){.pilcrow}

QUIC encodes transport parameters into a sequence of bytes, which is
then included in the cryptographic
handshake.[¶](#section-18-6){.pilcrow}

::: {#transport-parameter-grease}
::: {#section-18.1 .section}
### [18.1.](#section-18.1){.section-number .selfRef} [Reserved Transport Parameters](#name-reserved-transport-paramete){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-reserved-transport-paramete}

Transport parameters with an identifier of the form `31 * N + 27` for
integer values of N are reserved to exercise the requirement that
unknown transport parameters be ignored. These transport parameters have
no semantics and can carry arbitrary
values.[¶](#section-18.1-1){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#transport-parameter-definitions}
::: {#section-18.2 .section}
### [18.2.](#section-18.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Transport Parameter Definitions](#name-transport-parameter-definit){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-transport-parameter-definit}

This section details the transport parameters defined in this
document.[¶](#section-18.2-1){.pilcrow}

Many transport parameters listed here have integer values. Those
transport parameters that are identified as integers use a
variable-length integer encoding; see [Section
16](#integer-encoding){.xref}. Transport parameters have a default value
of 0 if the transport parameter is absent, unless otherwise
stated.[¶](#section-18.2-2){.pilcrow}

The following transport parameters are
defined:[¶](#section-18.2-3){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

original_destination_connection_id (0x00):

:   This parameter is the value of the Destination Connection ID field
    from the first Initial packet sent by the client; see [Section
    7.3](#cid-auth){.xref}. This transport parameter is only sent by a
    server.[¶](#section-18.2-4.2.1){.pilcrow}

:   

max_idle_timeout (0x01):

:   The maximum idle timeout is a value in milliseconds that is encoded
    as an integer; see ([Section 10.1](#idle-timeout){.xref}). Idle
    timeout is disabled when both endpoints omit this transport
    parameter or specify a value of 0.[¶](#section-18.2-4.4.1){.pilcrow}

:   

stateless_reset_token (0x02):

:   A stateless reset token is used in verifying a stateless reset; see
    [Section 10.3](#stateless-reset){.xref}. This parameter is a
    sequence of 16 bytes. This transport parameter [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} be
    sent by a client but [MAY]{.bcp14} be sent by a server. A server
    that does not send this transport parameter cannot use stateless
    reset ([Section 10.3](#stateless-reset){.xref}) for the connection
    ID negotiated during the
    handshake.[¶](#section-18.2-4.6.1){.pilcrow}

:   

max_udp_payload_size (0x03):

:   The maximum UDP payload size parameter is an integer value that
    limits the size of UDP payloads that the endpoint is willing to
    receive. UDP datagrams with payloads larger than this limit are not
    likely to be processed by the
    receiver.[¶](#section-18.2-4.8.1){.pilcrow}

:   

:   The default for this parameter is the maximum permitted UDP payload
    of 65527. Values below 1200 are
    invalid.[¶](#section-18.2-4.10.1){.pilcrow}

:   

:   This limit does act as an additional constraint on datagram size in
    the same way as the path MTU, but it is a property of the endpoint
    and not the path; see [Section 14](#datagram-size){.xref}. It is
    expected that this is the space an endpoint dedicates to holding
    incoming packets.[¶](#section-18.2-4.12.1){.pilcrow}

:   

initial_max_data (0x04):

:   The initial maximum data parameter is an integer value that contains
    the initial value for the maximum amount of data that can be sent on
    the connection. This is equivalent to sending a MAX_DATA ([Section
    19.9](#frame-max-data){.xref}) for the connection immediately after
    completing the handshake.[¶](#section-18.2-4.14.1){.pilcrow}

:   

initial_max_stream_data_bidi_local (0x05):

:   This parameter is an integer value specifying the initial flow
    control limit for locally initiated bidirectional streams. This
    limit applies to newly created bidirectional streams opened by the
    endpoint that sends the transport parameter. In client transport
    parameters, this applies to streams with an identifier with the
    least significant two bits set to 0x00; in server transport
    parameters, this applies to streams with the least significant two
    bits set to 0x01.[¶](#section-18.2-4.16.1){.pilcrow}

:   

initial_max_stream_data_bidi_remote (0x06):

:   This parameter is an integer value specifying the initial flow
    control limit for peer-initiated bidirectional streams. This limit
    applies to newly created bidirectional streams opened by the
    endpoint that receives the transport parameter. In client transport
    parameters, this applies to streams with an identifier with the
    least significant two bits set to 0x01; in server transport
    parameters, this applies to streams with the least significant two
    bits set to 0x00.[¶](#section-18.2-4.18.1){.pilcrow}

:   

initial_max_stream_data_uni (0x07):

:   This parameter is an integer value specifying the initial flow
    control limit for unidirectional streams. This limit applies to
    newly created unidirectional streams opened by the endpoint that
    receives the transport parameter. In client transport parameters,
    this applies to streams with an identifier with the least
    significant two bits set to 0x03; in server transport parameters,
    this applies to streams with the least significant two bits set to
    0x02.[¶](#section-18.2-4.20.1){.pilcrow}

:   

initial_max_streams_bidi (0x08):

:   The initial maximum bidirectional streams parameter is an integer
    value that contains the initial maximum number of bidirectional
    streams the endpoint that receives this transport parameter is
    permitted to initiate. If this parameter is absent or zero, the peer
    cannot open bidirectional streams until a MAX_STREAMS frame is sent.
    Setting this parameter is equivalent to sending a MAX_STREAMS
    ([Section 19.11](#frame-max-streams){.xref}) of the corresponding
    type with the same value.[¶](#section-18.2-4.22.1){.pilcrow}

:   

initial_max_streams_uni (0x09):

:   The initial maximum unidirectional streams parameter is an integer
    value that contains the initial maximum number of unidirectional
    streams the endpoint that receives this transport parameter is
    permitted to initiate. If this parameter is absent or zero, the peer
    cannot open unidirectional streams until a MAX_STREAMS frame is
    sent. Setting this parameter is equivalent to sending a MAX_STREAMS
    ([Section 19.11](#frame-max-streams){.xref}) of the corresponding
    type with the same value.[¶](#section-18.2-4.24.1){.pilcrow}

:   

ack_delay_exponent (0x0a):

:   The acknowledgment delay exponent is an integer value indicating an
    exponent used to decode the ACK Delay field in the ACK frame
    ([Section 19.3](#frame-ack){.xref}). If this value is absent, a
    default value of 3 is assumed (indicating a multiplier of 8). Values
    above 20 are invalid.[¶](#section-18.2-4.26.1){.pilcrow}

:   

max_ack_delay (0x0b):

:   The maximum acknowledgment delay is an integer value indicating the
    maximum amount of time in milliseconds by which the endpoint will
    delay sending acknowledgments. This value [SHOULD]{.bcp14} include
    the receiver\'s expected delays in alarms firing. For example, if a
    receiver sets a timer for 5ms and alarms commonly fire up to 1ms
    late, then it should send a max_ack_delay of 6ms. If this value is
    absent, a default of 25 milliseconds is assumed. Values of 2^14^ or
    greater are invalid.[¶](#section-18.2-4.28.1){.pilcrow}

:   

disable_active_migration (0x0c):

:   The disable active migration transport parameter is included if the
    endpoint does not support active connection migration ([Section
    9](#migration){.xref}) on the address being used during the
    handshake. An endpoint that receives this transport parameter [MUST
    NOT]{.bcp14} use a new local address when sending to the address
    that the peer used during the handshake. This transport parameter
    does not prohibit connection migration after a client has acted on a
    preferred_address transport parameter. This parameter is a
    zero-length value.[¶](#section-18.2-4.30.1){.pilcrow}

:   

preferred_address (0x0d):

:   The server\'s preferred address is used to effect a change in server
    address at the end of the handshake, as described in [Section
    9.6](#preferred-address){.xref}. This transport parameter is only
    sent by a server. Servers [MAY]{.bcp14} choose to only send a
    preferred address of one address family by sending an all-zero
    address and port (0.0.0.0:0 or \[::\]:0) for the other family. IP
    addresses are encoded in network byte
    order.[¶](#section-18.2-4.32.1){.pilcrow}

:   

:   The preferred_address transport parameter contains an address and
    port for both IPv4 and IPv6. The four-byte IPv4 Address field is
    followed by the associated two-byte IPv4 Port field. This is
    followed by a 16-byte IPv6 Address field and two-byte IPv6 Port
    field. After address and port pairs, a Connection ID Length field
    describes the length of the following Connection ID field. Finally,
    a 16-byte Stateless Reset Token field includes the stateless reset
    token associated with the connection ID. The format of this
    transport parameter is shown in [Figure
    22](#fig-preferred-address){.xref}
    below.[¶](#section-18.2-4.34.1){.pilcrow}

:   

:   The Connection ID field and the Stateless Reset Token field contain
    an alternative connection ID that has a sequence number of 1; see
    [Section 5.1.1](#issue-cid){.xref}. Having these values sent
    alongside the preferred address ensures that there will be at least
    one unused active connection ID when the client initiates migration
    to the preferred address.[¶](#section-18.2-4.36.1){.pilcrow}

:   

:   The Connection ID and Stateless Reset Token fields of a preferred
    address are identical in syntax and semantics to the corresponding
    fields of a NEW_CONNECTION_ID frame ([Section
    19.15](#frame-new-connection-id){.xref}). A server that chooses a
    zero-length connection ID [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} provide a preferred
    address. Similarly, a server [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} include a
    zero-length connection ID in this transport parameter. A client
    [MUST]{.bcp14} treat a violation of these requirements as a
    connection error of type
    TRANSPORT_PARAMETER_ERROR.[¶](#section-18.2-4.38.1){.pilcrow}

:   

[]{#name-preferred-address-format}

::: {#fig-preferred-address}
::: {#section-18.2-5.1 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
    Preferred Address {
      IPv4 Address (32),
      IPv4 Port (16),
      IPv6 Address (128),
      IPv6 Port (16),
      Connection ID Length (8),
      Connection ID (..),
      Stateless Reset Token (128),
    }
:::

[Figure 22](#figure-22){.selfRef}: [Preferred Address
Format](#name-preferred-address-format){.selfRef}
:::

[]{.break}

active_connection_id_limit (0x0e):

:   This is an integer value specifying the maximum number of connection
    IDs from the peer that an endpoint is willing to store. This value
    includes the connection ID received during the handshake, that
    received in the preferred_address transport parameter, and those
    received in NEW_CONNECTION_ID frames. The value of the
    active_connection_id_limit parameter [MUST]{.bcp14} be at least 2.
    An endpoint that receives a value less than 2 [MUST]{.bcp14} close
    the connection with an error of type TRANSPORT_PARAMETER_ERROR. If
    this transport parameter is absent, a default of 2 is assumed. If an
    endpoint issues a zero-length connection ID, it will never send a
    NEW_CONNECTION_ID frame and therefore ignores the
    active_connection_id_limit value received from its
    peer.[¶](#section-18.2-6.2.1){.pilcrow}

:   

initial_source_connection_id (0x0f):

:   This is the value that the endpoint included in the Source
    Connection ID field of the first Initial packet it sends for the
    connection; see [Section
    7.3](#cid-auth){.xref}.[¶](#section-18.2-6.4.1){.pilcrow}

:   

retry_source_connection_id (0x10):

:   This is the value that the server included in the Source Connection
    ID field of a Retry packet; see [Section 7.3](#cid-auth){.xref}.
    This transport parameter is only sent by a
    server.[¶](#section-18.2-6.6.1){.pilcrow}

:   

If present, transport parameters that set initial per-stream flow
control limits (initial_max_stream_data_bidi_local,
initial_max_stream_data_bidi_remote, and initial_max_stream_data_uni)
are equivalent to sending a MAX_STREAM_DATA frame ([Section
19.10](#frame-max-stream-data){.xref}) on every stream of the
corresponding type immediately after opening. If the transport parameter
is absent, streams of that type start with a flow control limit of
0.[¶](#section-18.2-7){.pilcrow}

A client [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} include any server-only transport parameter:
original_destination_connection_id, preferred_address,
retry_source_connection_id, or stateless_reset_token. A server
[MUST]{.bcp14} treat receipt of any of these transport parameters as a
connection error of type
TRANSPORT_PARAMETER_ERROR.[¶](#section-18.2-8){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
:::
:::

::: {#frame-formats}
::: {#section-19 .section}
## [19.](#section-19){.section-number .selfRef} [Frame Types and Formats](#name-frame-types-and-formats){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-frame-types-and-formats}

As described in [Section 12.4](#frames){.xref}, packets contain one or
more frames. This section describes the format and semantics of the core
QUIC frame types.[¶](#section-19-1){.pilcrow}

::: {#frame-padding}
::: {#section-19.1 .section}
### [19.1.](#section-19.1){.section-number .selfRef} [PADDING Frames](#name-padding-frames){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-padding-frames}

A PADDING frame (type=0x00) has no semantic value. PADDING frames can be
used to increase the size of a packet. Padding can be used to increase
an Initial packet to the minimum required size or to provide protection
against traffic analysis for protected
packets.[¶](#section-19.1-1){.pilcrow}

PADDING frames are formatted as shown in [Figure
23](#padding-format){.xref}, which shows that PADDING frames have no
content. That is, a PADDING frame consists of the single byte that
identifies the frame as a PADDING frame.[¶](#section-19.1-2){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-padding-frame-format}

::: {#padding-format}
::: {#section-19.1-3.1 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
    PADDING Frame {
      Type (i) = 0x00,
    }
:::

[Figure 23](#figure-23){.selfRef}: [PADDING Frame
Format](#name-padding-frame-format){.selfRef}
:::
:::
:::

::: {#frame-ping}
::: {#section-19.2 .section}
### [19.2.](#section-19.2){.section-number .selfRef} [PING Frames](#name-ping-frames){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-ping-frames}

Endpoints can use PING frames (type=0x01) to verify that their peers are
still alive or to check reachability to the
peer.[¶](#section-19.2-1){.pilcrow}

PING frames are formatted as shown in [Figure 24](#ping-format){.xref},
which shows that PING frames have no
content.[¶](#section-19.2-2){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-ping-frame-format}

::: {#ping-format}
::: {#section-19.2-3.1 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
    PING Frame {
      Type (i) = 0x01,
    }
:::

[Figure 24](#figure-24){.selfRef}: [PING Frame
Format](#name-ping-frame-format){.selfRef}
:::

The receiver of a PING frame simply needs to acknowledge the packet
containing this frame.[¶](#section-19.2-4){.pilcrow}

The PING frame can be used to keep a connection alive when an
application or application protocol wishes to prevent the connection
from timing out; see [Section
10.1.2](#defer-idle){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.2-5){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#frame-ack}
::: {#section-19.3 .section}
### [19.3.](#section-19.3){.section-number .selfRef} [ACK Frames](#name-ack-frames){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-ack-frames}

Receivers send ACK frames (types 0x02 and 0x03) to inform senders of
packets they have received and processed. The ACK frame contains one or
more ACK Ranges. ACK Ranges identify acknowledged packets. If the frame
type is 0x03, ACK frames also contain the cumulative count of QUIC
packets with associated ECN marks received on the connection up until
this point. QUIC implementations [MUST]{.bcp14} properly handle both
types, and, if they have enabled ECN for packets they send, they
[SHOULD]{.bcp14} use the information in the ECN section to manage their
congestion state.[¶](#section-19.3-1){.pilcrow}

QUIC acknowledgments are irrevocable. Once acknowledged, a packet
remains acknowledged, even if it does not appear in a future ACK frame.
This is unlike reneging for TCP Selective Acknowledgments (SACKs)
\[[RFC2018](#RFC2018){.xref}\].[¶](#section-19.3-2){.pilcrow}

Packets from different packet number spaces can be identified using the
same numeric value. An acknowledgment for a packet needs to indicate
both a packet number and a packet number space. This is accomplished by
having each ACK frame only acknowledge packet numbers in the same space
as the packet in which the ACK frame is
contained.[¶](#section-19.3-3){.pilcrow}

Version Negotiation and Retry packets cannot be acknowledged because
they do not contain a packet number. Rather than relying on ACK frames,
these packets are implicitly acknowledged by the next Initial packet
sent by the client.[¶](#section-19.3-4){.pilcrow}

ACK frames are formatted as shown in [Figure
25](#ack-format){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.3-5){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-ack-frame-format}

::: {#ack-format}
::: {#section-19.3-6.1 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
    ACK Frame {
      Type (i) = 0x02..0x03,
      Largest Acknowledged (i),
      ACK Delay (i),
      ACK Range Count (i),
      First ACK Range (i),
      ACK Range (..) ...,
      [ECN Counts (..)],
    }
:::

[Figure 25](#figure-25){.selfRef}: [ACK Frame
Format](#name-ack-frame-format){.selfRef}
:::

ACK frames contain the following fields:[¶](#section-19.3-7){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Largest Acknowledged:

:   A variable-length integer representing the largest packet number the
    peer is acknowledging; this is usually the largest packet number
    that the peer has received prior to generating the ACK frame. Unlike
    the packet number in the QUIC long or short header, the value in an
    ACK frame is not truncated.[¶](#section-19.3-8.2.1){.pilcrow}

:   

ACK Delay:

:   A variable-length integer encoding the acknowledgment delay in
    microseconds; see [Section 13.2.5](#host-delay){.xref}. It is
    decoded by multiplying the value in the field by 2 to the power of
    the ack_delay_exponent transport parameter sent by the sender of the
    ACK frame; see [Section
    18.2](#transport-parameter-definitions){.xref}. Compared to simply
    expressing the delay as an integer, this encoding allows for a
    larger range of values within the same number of bytes, at the cost
    of lower resolution.[¶](#section-19.3-8.4.1){.pilcrow}

:   

ACK Range Count:

:   A variable-length integer specifying the number of ACK Range fields
    in the frame.[¶](#section-19.3-8.6.1){.pilcrow}

:   

First ACK Range:

:   A variable-length integer indicating the number of contiguous
    packets preceding the Largest Acknowledged that are being
    acknowledged. That is, the smallest packet acknowledged in the range
    is determined by subtracting the First ACK Range value from the
    Largest Acknowledged field.[¶](#section-19.3-8.8.1){.pilcrow}

:   

ACK Ranges:

:   Contains additional ranges of packets that are alternately not
    acknowledged (Gap) and acknowledged (ACK Range); see [Section
    19.3.1](#ack-ranges){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.3-8.10.1){.pilcrow}

:   

ECN Counts:

:   The three ECN counts; see [Section
    19.3.2](#ack-ecn-counts){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.3-8.12.1){.pilcrow}

:   

::: {#ack-ranges}
::: {#section-19.3.1 .section}
#### [19.3.1.](#section-19.3.1){.section-number .selfRef} [ACK Ranges](#name-ack-ranges){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-ack-ranges}

Each ACK Range consists of alternating Gap and ACK Range Length values
in descending packet number order. ACK Ranges can be repeated. The
number of Gap and ACK Range Length values is determined by the ACK Range
Count field; one of each value is present for each value in the ACK
Range Count field.[¶](#section-19.3.1-1){.pilcrow}

ACK Ranges are structured as shown in [Figure
26](#ack-range-format){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.3.1-2){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-ack-ranges-2}

::: {#ack-range-format}
::: {#section-19.3.1-3.1 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
    ACK Range {
      Gap (i),
      ACK Range Length (i),
    }
:::

[Figure 26](#figure-26){.selfRef}: [ACK
Ranges](#name-ack-ranges-2){.selfRef}
:::

The fields that form each ACK Range are:[¶](#section-19.3.1-4){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Gap:

:   A variable-length integer indicating the number of contiguous
    unacknowledged packets preceding the packet number one lower than
    the smallest in the preceding ACK
    Range.[¶](#section-19.3.1-5.2.1){.pilcrow}

:   

ACK Range Length:

:   A variable-length integer indicating the number of contiguous
    acknowledged packets preceding the largest packet number, as
    determined by the preceding Gap.[¶](#section-19.3.1-5.4.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Gap and ACK Range Length values use a relative integer encoding for
efficiency. Though each encoded value is positive, the values are
subtracted, so that each ACK Range describes progressively
lower-numbered packets.[¶](#section-19.3.1-6){.pilcrow}

Each ACK Range acknowledges a contiguous range of packets by indicating
the number of acknowledged packets that precede the largest packet
number in that range. A value of 0 indicates that only the largest
packet number is acknowledged. Larger ACK Range values indicate a larger
range, with corresponding lower values for the smallest packet number in
the range. Thus, given a largest packet number for the range, the
smallest value is determined by the following
formula:[¶](#section-19.3.1-7){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-19.3.1-8 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
       smallest = largest - ack_range

[¶](#section-19.3.1-8){.pilcrow}
:::

An ACK Range acknowledges all packets between the smallest packet number
and the largest, inclusive.[¶](#section-19.3.1-9){.pilcrow}

The largest value for an ACK Range is determined by cumulatively
subtracting the size of all preceding ACK Range Lengths and
Gaps.[¶](#section-19.3.1-10){.pilcrow}

Each Gap indicates a range of packets that are not being acknowledged.
The number of packets in the gap is one higher than the encoded value of
the Gap field.[¶](#section-19.3.1-11){.pilcrow}

The value of the Gap field establishes the largest packet number value
for the subsequent ACK Range using the following
formula:[¶](#section-19.3.1-12){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-19.3.1-13 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
       largest = previous_smallest - gap - 2

[¶](#section-19.3.1-13){.pilcrow}
:::

If any computed packet number is negative, an endpoint [MUST]{.bcp14}
generate a connection error of type
FRAME_ENCODING_ERROR.[¶](#section-19.3.1-14){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#ack-ecn-counts}
::: {#section-19.3.2 .section}
#### [19.3.2.](#section-19.3.2){.section-number .selfRef} [ECN Counts](#name-ecn-counts){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-ecn-counts}

The ACK frame uses the least significant bit of the type value (that is,
type 0x03) to indicate ECN feedback and report receipt of QUIC packets
with associated ECN codepoints of ECT(0), ECT(1), or ECN-CE in the
packet\'s IP header. ECN counts are only present when the ACK frame type
is 0x03.[¶](#section-19.3.2-1){.pilcrow}

When present, there are three ECN counts, as shown in [Figure
27](#ecn-count-format){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.3.2-2){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-ecn-count-format}

::: {#ecn-count-format}
::: {#section-19.3.2-3.1 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
    ECN Counts {
      ECT0 Count (i),
      ECT1 Count (i),
      ECN-CE Count (i),
    }
:::

[Figure 27](#figure-27){.selfRef}: [ECN Count
Format](#name-ecn-count-format){.selfRef}
:::

The ECN count fields are:[¶](#section-19.3.2-4){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

ECT0 Count:

:   A variable-length integer representing the total number of packets
    received with the ECT(0) codepoint in the packet number space of the
    ACK frame.[¶](#section-19.3.2-5.2.1){.pilcrow}

:   

ECT1 Count:

:   A variable-length integer representing the total number of packets
    received with the ECT(1) codepoint in the packet number space of the
    ACK frame.[¶](#section-19.3.2-5.4.1){.pilcrow}

:   

ECN-CE Count:

:   A variable-length integer representing the total number of packets
    received with the ECN-CE codepoint in the packet number space of the
    ACK frame.[¶](#section-19.3.2-5.6.1){.pilcrow}

:   

ECN counts are maintained separately for each packet number
space.[¶](#section-19.3.2-6){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
:::
:::

::: {#frame-reset-stream}
::: {#section-19.4 .section}
### [19.4.](#section-19.4){.section-number .selfRef} [RESET_STREAM Frames](#name-reset_stream-frames){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-reset_stream-frames}

An endpoint uses a RESET_STREAM frame (type=0x04) to abruptly terminate
the sending part of a stream.[¶](#section-19.4-1){.pilcrow}

After sending a RESET_STREAM, an endpoint ceases transmission and
retransmission of STREAM frames on the identified stream. A receiver of
RESET_STREAM can discard any data that it already received on that
stream.[¶](#section-19.4-2){.pilcrow}

An endpoint that receives a RESET_STREAM frame for a send-only stream
[MUST]{.bcp14} terminate the connection with error
STREAM_STATE_ERROR.[¶](#section-19.4-3){.pilcrow}

RESET_STREAM frames are formatted as shown in [Figure
28](#fig-reset-stream){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.4-4){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-reset_stream-frame-format}

::: {#fig-reset-stream}
::: {#section-19.4-5.1 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
    RESET_STREAM Frame {
      Type (i) = 0x04,
      Stream ID (i),
      Application Protocol Error Code (i),
      Final Size (i),
    }
:::

[Figure 28](#figure-28){.selfRef}: [RESET_STREAM Frame
Format](#name-reset_stream-frame-format){.selfRef}
:::

RESET_STREAM frames contain the following
fields:[¶](#section-19.4-6){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Stream ID:

:   A variable-length integer encoding of the stream ID of the stream
    being terminated.[¶](#section-19.4-7.2.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Application Protocol Error Code:

:   A variable-length integer containing the application protocol error
    code (see [Section 20.2](#app-error-codes){.xref}) that indicates
    why the stream is being closed.[¶](#section-19.4-7.4.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Final Size:

:   A variable-length integer indicating the final size of the stream by
    the RESET_STREAM sender, in units of bytes; see [Section
    4.5](#final-size){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.4-7.6.1){.pilcrow}

:   
:::
:::

::: {#frame-stop-sending}
::: {#section-19.5 .section}
### [19.5.](#section-19.5){.section-number .selfRef} [STOP_SENDING Frames](#name-stop_sending-frames){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-stop_sending-frames}

An endpoint uses a STOP_SENDING frame (type=0x05) to communicate that
incoming data is being discarded on receipt per application request.
STOP_SENDING requests that a peer cease transmission on a
stream.[¶](#section-19.5-1){.pilcrow}

A STOP_SENDING frame can be sent for streams in the \"Recv\" or \"Size
Known\" states; see [Section 3.2](#stream-recv-states){.xref}. Receiving
a STOP_SENDING frame for a locally initiated stream that has not yet
been created [MUST]{.bcp14} be treated as a connection error of type
STREAM_STATE_ERROR. An endpoint that receives a STOP_SENDING frame for a
receive-only stream [MUST]{.bcp14} terminate the connection with error
STREAM_STATE_ERROR.[¶](#section-19.5-2){.pilcrow}

STOP_SENDING frames are formatted as shown in [Figure
29](#fig-stop-sending){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.5-3){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-stop_sending-frame-format}

::: {#fig-stop-sending}
::: {#section-19.5-4.1 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
    STOP_SENDING Frame {
      Type (i) = 0x05,
      Stream ID (i),
      Application Protocol Error Code (i),
    }
:::

[Figure 29](#figure-29){.selfRef}: [STOP_SENDING Frame
Format](#name-stop_sending-frame-format){.selfRef}
:::

STOP_SENDING frames contain the following
fields:[¶](#section-19.5-5){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Stream ID:

:   A variable-length integer carrying the stream ID of the stream being
    ignored.[¶](#section-19.5-6.2.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Application Protocol Error Code:

:   A variable-length integer containing the application-specified
    reason the sender is ignoring the stream; see [Section
    20.2](#app-error-codes){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.5-6.4.1){.pilcrow}

:   
:::
:::

::: {#frame-crypto}
::: {#section-19.6 .section}
### [19.6.](#section-19.6){.section-number .selfRef} [CRYPTO Frames](#name-crypto-frames){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-crypto-frames}

A CRYPTO frame (type=0x06) is used to transmit cryptographic handshake
messages. It can be sent in all packet types except 0-RTT. The CRYPTO
frame offers the cryptographic protocol an in-order stream of bytes.
CRYPTO frames are functionally identical to STREAM frames, except that
they do not bear a stream identifier; they are not flow controlled; and
they do not carry markers for optional offset, optional length, and the
end of the stream.[¶](#section-19.6-1){.pilcrow}

CRYPTO frames are formatted as shown in [Figure
30](#fig-crypto){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.6-2){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-crypto-frame-format}

::: {#fig-crypto}
::: {#section-19.6-3.1 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
    CRYPTO Frame {
      Type (i) = 0x06,
      Offset (i),
      Length (i),
      Crypto Data (..),
    }
:::

[Figure 30](#figure-30){.selfRef}: [CRYPTO Frame
Format](#name-crypto-frame-format){.selfRef}
:::

CRYPTO frames contain the following
fields:[¶](#section-19.6-4){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Offset:

:   A variable-length integer specifying the byte offset in the stream
    for the data in this CRYPTO frame.[¶](#section-19.6-5.2.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Length:

:   A variable-length integer specifying the length of the Crypto Data
    field in this CRYPTO frame.[¶](#section-19.6-5.4.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Crypto Data:

:   The cryptographic message data.[¶](#section-19.6-5.6.1){.pilcrow}

:   

There is a separate flow of cryptographic handshake data in each
encryption level, each of which starts at an offset of 0. This implies
that each encryption level is treated as a separate CRYPTO stream of
data.[¶](#section-19.6-6){.pilcrow}

The largest offset delivered on a stream \-- the sum of the offset and
data length \-- cannot exceed 2^62^-1. Receipt of a frame that exceeds
this limit [MUST]{.bcp14} be treated as a connection error of type
FRAME_ENCODING_ERROR or
CRYPTO_BUFFER_EXCEEDED.[¶](#section-19.6-7){.pilcrow}

Unlike STREAM frames, which include a stream ID indicating to which
stream the data belongs, the CRYPTO frame carries data for a single
stream per encryption level. The stream does not have an explicit end,
so CRYPTO frames do not have a FIN bit.[¶](#section-19.6-8){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#frame-new-token}
::: {#section-19.7 .section}
### [19.7.](#section-19.7){.section-number .selfRef} [NEW_TOKEN Frames](#name-new_token-frames){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-new_token-frames}

A server sends a NEW_TOKEN frame (type=0x07) to provide the client with
a token to send in the header of an Initial packet for a future
connection.[¶](#section-19.7-1){.pilcrow}

NEW_TOKEN frames are formatted as shown in [Figure
31](#fig-new-token){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.7-2){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-new_token-frame-format}

::: {#fig-new-token}
::: {#section-19.7-3.1 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
    NEW_TOKEN Frame {
      Type (i) = 0x07,
      Token Length (i),
      Token (..),
    }
:::

[Figure 31](#figure-31){.selfRef}: [NEW_TOKEN Frame
Format](#name-new_token-frame-format){.selfRef}
:::

NEW_TOKEN frames contain the following
fields:[¶](#section-19.7-4){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Token Length:

:   A variable-length integer specifying the length of the token in
    bytes.[¶](#section-19.7-5.2.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Token:

:   An opaque blob that the client can use with a future Initial packet.
    The token [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} be empty. A client [MUST]{.bcp14} treat
    receipt of a NEW_TOKEN frame with an empty Token field as a
    connection error of type
    FRAME_ENCODING_ERROR.[¶](#section-19.7-5.4.1){.pilcrow}

:   

A client might receive multiple NEW_TOKEN frames that contain the same
token value if packets containing the frame are incorrectly determined
to be lost. Clients are responsible for discarding duplicate values,
which might be used to link connection attempts; see [Section
8.1.3](#validate-future){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.7-6){.pilcrow}

Clients [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} send NEW_TOKEN frames. A server
[MUST]{.bcp14} treat receipt of a NEW_TOKEN frame as a connection error
of type PROTOCOL_VIOLATION.[¶](#section-19.7-7){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#frame-stream}
::: {#section-19.8 .section}
### [19.8.](#section-19.8){.section-number .selfRef} [STREAM Frames](#name-stream-frames){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-stream-frames}

STREAM frames implicitly create a stream and carry stream data. The Type
field in the STREAM frame takes the form 0b00001XXX (or the set of
values from 0x08 to 0x0f). The three low-order bits of the frame type
determine the fields that are present in the
frame:[¶](#section-19.8-1){.pilcrow}

-   [The OFF bit (0x04) in the frame type is set to indicate that there
    is an Offset field present. When set to 1, the Offset field is
    present. When set to 0, the Offset field is absent and the Stream
    Data starts at an offset of 0 (that is, the frame contains the first
    bytes of the stream, or the end of a stream that includes no
    data).[¶](#section-19.8-2.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-19.8-2.1}
-   [The LEN bit (0x02) in the frame type is set to indicate that there
    is a Length field present. If this bit is set to 0, the Length field
    is absent and the Stream Data field extends to the end of the
    packet. If this bit is set to 1, the Length field is
    present.[¶](#section-19.8-2.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-19.8-2.2}
-   [The FIN bit (0x01) indicates that the frame marks the end of the
    stream. The final size of the stream is the sum of the offset and
    the length of this
    frame.[¶](#section-19.8-2.3){.pilcrow}]{#section-19.8-2.3}

An endpoint [MUST]{.bcp14} terminate the connection with error
STREAM_STATE_ERROR if it receives a STREAM frame for a locally initiated
stream that has not yet been created, or for a send-only
stream.[¶](#section-19.8-3){.pilcrow}

STREAM frames are formatted as shown in [Figure
32](#fig-stream){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.8-4){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-stream-frame-format}

::: {#fig-stream}
::: {#section-19.8-5.1 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
    STREAM Frame {
      Type (i) = 0x08..0x0f,
      Stream ID (i),
      [Offset (i)],
      [Length (i)],
      Stream Data (..),
    }
:::

[Figure 32](#figure-32){.selfRef}: [STREAM Frame
Format](#name-stream-frame-format){.selfRef}
:::

STREAM frames contain the following
fields:[¶](#section-19.8-6){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Stream ID:

:   A variable-length integer indicating the stream ID of the stream;
    see [Section
    2.1](#stream-id){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.8-7.2.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Offset:

:   A variable-length integer specifying the byte offset in the stream
    for the data in this STREAM frame. This field is present when the
    OFF bit is set to 1. When the Offset field is absent, the offset is
    0.[¶](#section-19.8-7.4.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Length:

:   A variable-length integer specifying the length of the Stream Data
    field in this STREAM frame. This field is present when the LEN bit
    is set to 1. When the LEN bit is set to 0, the Stream Data field
    consumes all the remaining bytes in the
    packet.[¶](#section-19.8-7.6.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Stream Data:

:   The bytes from the designated stream to be
    delivered.[¶](#section-19.8-7.8.1){.pilcrow}

:   

When a Stream Data field has a length of 0, the offset in the STREAM
frame is the offset of the next byte that would be
sent.[¶](#section-19.8-8){.pilcrow}

The first byte in the stream has an offset of 0. The largest offset
delivered on a stream \-- the sum of the offset and data length \--
cannot exceed 2^62^-1, as it is not possible to provide flow control
credit for that data. Receipt of a frame that exceeds this limit
[MUST]{.bcp14} be treated as a connection error of type
FRAME_ENCODING_ERROR or
FLOW_CONTROL_ERROR.[¶](#section-19.8-9){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#frame-max-data}
::: {#section-19.9 .section}
### [19.9.](#section-19.9){.section-number .selfRef} [MAX_DATA Frames](#name-max_data-frames){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-max_data-frames}

A MAX_DATA frame (type=0x10) is used in flow control to inform the peer
of the maximum amount of data that can be sent on the connection as a
whole.[¶](#section-19.9-1){.pilcrow}

MAX_DATA frames are formatted as shown in [Figure
33](#fig-max-data){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.9-2){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-max_data-frame-format}

::: {#fig-max-data}
::: {#section-19.9-3.1 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
    MAX_DATA Frame {
      Type (i) = 0x10,
      Maximum Data (i),
    }
:::

[Figure 33](#figure-33){.selfRef}: [MAX_DATA Frame
Format](#name-max_data-frame-format){.selfRef}
:::

MAX_DATA frames contain the following
field:[¶](#section-19.9-4){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Maximum Data:

:   A variable-length integer indicating the maximum amount of data that
    can be sent on the entire connection, in units of
    bytes.[¶](#section-19.9-5.2.1){.pilcrow}

:   

All data sent in STREAM frames counts toward this limit. The sum of the
final sizes on all streams \-- including streams in terminal states \--
[MUST NOT]{.bcp14} exceed the value advertised by a receiver. An
endpoint [MUST]{.bcp14} terminate a connection with an error of type
FLOW_CONTROL_ERROR if it receives more data than the maximum data value
that it has sent. This includes violations of remembered limits in Early
Data; see [Section
7.4.1](#zerortt-parameters){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.9-6){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#frame-max-stream-data}
::: {#section-19.10 .section}
### [19.10.](#section-19.10){.section-number .selfRef} [MAX_STREAM_DATA Frames](#name-max_stream_data-frames){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-max_stream_data-frames}

A MAX_STREAM_DATA frame (type=0x11) is used in flow control to inform a
peer of the maximum amount of data that can be sent on a
stream.[¶](#section-19.10-1){.pilcrow}

A MAX_STREAM_DATA frame can be sent for streams in the \"Recv\" state;
see [Section 3.2](#stream-recv-states){.xref}. Receiving a
MAX_STREAM_DATA frame for a locally initiated stream that has not yet
been created [MUST]{.bcp14} be treated as a connection error of type
STREAM_STATE_ERROR. An endpoint that receives a MAX_STREAM_DATA frame
for a receive-only stream [MUST]{.bcp14} terminate the connection with
error STREAM_STATE_ERROR.[¶](#section-19.10-2){.pilcrow}

MAX_STREAM_DATA frames are formatted as shown in [Figure
34](#fig-max-stream-data){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.10-3){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-max_stream_data-frame-forma}

::: {#fig-max-stream-data}
::: {#section-19.10-4.1 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
    MAX_STREAM_DATA Frame {
      Type (i) = 0x11,
      Stream ID (i),
      Maximum Stream Data (i),
    }
:::

[Figure 34](#figure-34){.selfRef}: [MAX_STREAM_DATA Frame
Format](#name-max_stream_data-frame-forma){.selfRef}
:::

MAX_STREAM_DATA frames contain the following
fields:[¶](#section-19.10-5){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Stream ID:

:   The stream ID of the affected stream, encoded as a variable-length
    integer.[¶](#section-19.10-6.2.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Maximum Stream Data:

:   A variable-length integer indicating the maximum amount of data that
    can be sent on the identified stream, in units of
    bytes.[¶](#section-19.10-6.4.1){.pilcrow}

:   

When counting data toward this limit, an endpoint accounts for the
largest received offset of data that is sent or received on the stream.
Loss or reordering can mean that the largest received offset on a stream
can be greater than the total size of data received on that stream.
Receiving STREAM frames might not increase the largest received
offset.[¶](#section-19.10-7){.pilcrow}

The data sent on a stream [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} exceed the largest maximum
stream data value advertised by the receiver. An endpoint [MUST]{.bcp14}
terminate a connection with an error of type FLOW_CONTROL_ERROR if it
receives more data than the largest maximum stream data that it has sent
for the affected stream. This includes violations of remembered limits
in Early Data; see [Section
7.4.1](#zerortt-parameters){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.10-8){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#frame-max-streams}
::: {#section-19.11 .section}
### [19.11.](#section-19.11){.section-number .selfRef} [MAX_STREAMS Frames](#name-max_streams-frames){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-max_streams-frames}

A MAX_STREAMS frame (type=0x12 or 0x13) informs the peer of the
cumulative number of streams of a given type it is permitted to open. A
MAX_STREAMS frame with a type of 0x12 applies to bidirectional streams,
and a MAX_STREAMS frame with a type of 0x13 applies to unidirectional
streams.[¶](#section-19.11-1){.pilcrow}

MAX_STREAMS frames are formatted as shown in [Figure
35](#fig-max-streams){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.11-2){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-max_streams-frame-format}

::: {#fig-max-streams}
::: {#section-19.11-3.1 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
    MAX_STREAMS Frame {
      Type (i) = 0x12..0x13,
      Maximum Streams (i),
    }
:::

[Figure 35](#figure-35){.selfRef}: [MAX_STREAMS Frame
Format](#name-max_streams-frame-format){.selfRef}
:::

MAX_STREAMS frames contain the following
field:[¶](#section-19.11-4){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Maximum Streams:

:   A count of the cumulative number of streams of the corresponding
    type that can be opened over the lifetime of the connection. This
    value cannot exceed 2^60^, as it is not possible to encode stream
    IDs larger than 2^62^-1. Receipt of a frame that permits opening of
    a stream larger than this limit [MUST]{.bcp14} be treated as a
    connection error of type
    FRAME_ENCODING_ERROR.[¶](#section-19.11-5.2.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Loss or reordering can cause an endpoint to receive a MAX_STREAMS frame
with a lower stream limit than was previously received. MAX_STREAMS
frames that do not increase the stream limit [MUST]{.bcp14} be
ignored.[¶](#section-19.11-6){.pilcrow}

An endpoint [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} open more streams than permitted by the
current stream limit set by its peer. For instance, a server that
receives a unidirectional stream limit of 3 is permitted to open streams
3, 7, and 11, but not stream 15. An endpoint [MUST]{.bcp14} terminate a
connection with an error of type STREAM_LIMIT_ERROR if a peer opens more
streams than was permitted. This includes violations of remembered
limits in Early Data; see [Section
7.4.1](#zerortt-parameters){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.11-7){.pilcrow}

Note that these frames (and the corresponding transport parameters) do
not describe the number of streams that can be opened concurrently. The
limit includes streams that have been closed as well as those that are
open.[¶](#section-19.11-8){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#frame-data-blocked}
::: {#section-19.12 .section}
### [19.12.](#section-19.12){.section-number .selfRef} [DATA_BLOCKED Frames](#name-data_blocked-frames){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-data_blocked-frames}

A sender [SHOULD]{.bcp14} send a DATA_BLOCKED frame (type=0x14) when it
wishes to send data but is unable to do so due to connection-level flow
control; see [Section 4](#flow-control){.xref}. DATA_BLOCKED frames can
be used as input to tuning of flow control algorithms; see [Section
4.2](#fc-credit){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.12-1){.pilcrow}

DATA_BLOCKED frames are formatted as shown in [Figure
36](#fig-data-blocked){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.12-2){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-data_blocked-frame-format}

::: {#fig-data-blocked}
::: {#section-19.12-3.1 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
    DATA_BLOCKED Frame {
      Type (i) = 0x14,
      Maximum Data (i),
    }
:::

[Figure 36](#figure-36){.selfRef}: [DATA_BLOCKED Frame
Format](#name-data_blocked-frame-format){.selfRef}
:::

DATA_BLOCKED frames contain the following
field:[¶](#section-19.12-4){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Maximum Data:

:   A variable-length integer indicating the connection-level limit at
    which blocking occurred.[¶](#section-19.12-5.2.1){.pilcrow}

:   
:::
:::

::: {#frame-stream-data-blocked}
::: {#section-19.13 .section}
### [19.13.](#section-19.13){.section-number .selfRef} [STREAM_DATA_BLOCKED Frames](#name-stream_data_blocked-frames){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-stream_data_blocked-frames}

A sender [SHOULD]{.bcp14} send a STREAM_DATA_BLOCKED frame (type=0x15)
when it wishes to send data but is unable to do so due to stream-level
flow control. This frame is analogous to DATA_BLOCKED ([Section
19.12](#frame-data-blocked){.xref}).[¶](#section-19.13-1){.pilcrow}

An endpoint that receives a STREAM_DATA_BLOCKED frame for a send-only
stream [MUST]{.bcp14} terminate the connection with error
STREAM_STATE_ERROR.[¶](#section-19.13-2){.pilcrow}

STREAM_DATA_BLOCKED frames are formatted as shown in [Figure
37](#fig-stream-data-blocked){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.13-3){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-stream_data_blocked-frame-f}

::: {#fig-stream-data-blocked}
::: {#section-19.13-4.1 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
    STREAM_DATA_BLOCKED Frame {
      Type (i) = 0x15,
      Stream ID (i),
      Maximum Stream Data (i),
    }
:::

[Figure 37](#figure-37){.selfRef}: [STREAM_DATA_BLOCKED Frame
Format](#name-stream_data_blocked-frame-f){.selfRef}
:::

STREAM_DATA_BLOCKED frames contain the following
fields:[¶](#section-19.13-5){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Stream ID:

:   A variable-length integer indicating the stream that is blocked due
    to flow control.[¶](#section-19.13-6.2.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Maximum Stream Data:

:   A variable-length integer indicating the offset of the stream at
    which the blocking occurred.[¶](#section-19.13-6.4.1){.pilcrow}

:   
:::
:::

::: {#frame-streams-blocked}
::: {#section-19.14 .section}
### [19.14.](#section-19.14){.section-number .selfRef} [STREAMS_BLOCKED Frames](#name-streams_blocked-frames){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-streams_blocked-frames}

A sender [SHOULD]{.bcp14} send a STREAMS_BLOCKED frame (type=0x16 or
0x17) when it wishes to open a stream but is unable to do so due to the
maximum stream limit set by its peer; see [Section
19.11](#frame-max-streams){.xref}. A STREAMS_BLOCKED frame of type 0x16
is used to indicate reaching the bidirectional stream limit, and a
STREAMS_BLOCKED frame of type 0x17 is used to indicate reaching the
unidirectional stream limit.[¶](#section-19.14-1){.pilcrow}

A STREAMS_BLOCKED frame does not open the stream, but informs the peer
that a new stream was needed and the stream limit prevented the creation
of the stream.[¶](#section-19.14-2){.pilcrow}

STREAMS_BLOCKED frames are formatted as shown in [Figure
38](#fig-streams-blocked){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.14-3){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-streams_blocked-frame-forma}

::: {#fig-streams-blocked}
::: {#section-19.14-4.1 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
    STREAMS_BLOCKED Frame {
      Type (i) = 0x16..0x17,
      Maximum Streams (i),
    }
:::

[Figure 38](#figure-38){.selfRef}: [STREAMS_BLOCKED Frame
Format](#name-streams_blocked-frame-forma){.selfRef}
:::

STREAMS_BLOCKED frames contain the following
field:[¶](#section-19.14-5){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Maximum Streams:

:   A variable-length integer indicating the maximum number of streams
    allowed at the time the frame was sent. This value cannot exceed
    2^60^, as it is not possible to encode stream IDs larger than
    2^62^-1. Receipt of a frame that encodes a larger stream ID
    [MUST]{.bcp14} be treated as a connection error of type
    STREAM_LIMIT_ERROR or
    FRAME_ENCODING_ERROR.[¶](#section-19.14-6.2.1){.pilcrow}

:   
:::
:::

::: {#frame-new-connection-id}
::: {#section-19.15 .section}
### [19.15.](#section-19.15){.section-number .selfRef} [NEW_CONNECTION_ID Frames](#name-new_connection_id-frames){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-new_connection_id-frames}

An endpoint sends a NEW_CONNECTION_ID frame (type=0x18) to provide its
peer with alternative connection IDs that can be used to break
linkability when migrating connections; see [Section
9.5](#migration-linkability){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.15-1){.pilcrow}

NEW_CONNECTION_ID frames are formatted as shown in [Figure
39](#fig-new-connection-id){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.15-2){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-new_connection_id-frame-for}

::: {#fig-new-connection-id}
::: {#section-19.15-3.1 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
    NEW_CONNECTION_ID Frame {
      Type (i) = 0x18,
      Sequence Number (i),
      Retire Prior To (i),
      Length (8),
      Connection ID (8..160),
      Stateless Reset Token (128),
    }
:::

[Figure 39](#figure-39){.selfRef}: [NEW_CONNECTION_ID Frame
Format](#name-new_connection_id-frame-for){.selfRef}
:::

NEW_CONNECTION_ID frames contain the following
fields:[¶](#section-19.15-4){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Sequence Number:

:   The sequence number assigned to the connection ID by the sender,
    encoded as a variable-length integer; see [Section
    5.1.1](#issue-cid){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.15-5.2.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Retire Prior To:

:   A variable-length integer indicating which connection IDs should be
    retired; see [Section
    5.1.2](#retire-cid){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.15-5.4.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Length:

:   An 8-bit unsigned integer containing the length of the connection
    ID. Values less than 1 and greater than 20 are invalid and
    [MUST]{.bcp14} be treated as a connection error of type
    FRAME_ENCODING_ERROR.[¶](#section-19.15-5.6.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Connection ID:

:   A connection ID of the specified
    length.[¶](#section-19.15-5.8.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Stateless Reset Token:

:   A 128-bit value that will be used for a stateless reset when the
    associated connection ID is used; see [Section
    10.3](#stateless-reset){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.15-5.10.1){.pilcrow}

:   

An endpoint [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} send this frame if it currently requires
that its peer send packets with a zero-length Destination Connection ID.
Changing the length of a connection ID to or from zero length makes it
difficult to identify when the value of the connection ID changed. An
endpoint that is sending packets with a zero-length Destination
Connection ID [MUST]{.bcp14} treat receipt of a NEW_CONNECTION_ID frame
as a connection error of type
PROTOCOL_VIOLATION.[¶](#section-19.15-6){.pilcrow}

Transmission errors, timeouts, and retransmissions might cause the same
NEW_CONNECTION_ID frame to be received multiple times. Receipt of the
same frame multiple times [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} be treated as a connection
error. A receiver can use the sequence number supplied in the
NEW_CONNECTION_ID frame to handle receiving the same NEW_CONNECTION_ID
frame multiple times.[¶](#section-19.15-7){.pilcrow}

If an endpoint receives a NEW_CONNECTION_ID frame that repeats a
previously issued connection ID with a different Stateless Reset Token
field value or a different Sequence Number field value, or if a sequence
number is used for different connection IDs, the endpoint [MAY]{.bcp14}
treat that receipt as a connection error of type
PROTOCOL_VIOLATION.[¶](#section-19.15-8){.pilcrow}

The Retire Prior To field applies to connection IDs established during
connection setup and the preferred_address transport parameter; see
[Section 5.1.2](#retire-cid){.xref}. The value in the Retire Prior To
field [MUST]{.bcp14} be less than or equal to the value in the Sequence
Number field. Receiving a value in the Retire Prior To field that is
greater than that in the Sequence Number field [MUST]{.bcp14} be treated
as a connection error of type
FRAME_ENCODING_ERROR.[¶](#section-19.15-9){.pilcrow}

Once a sender indicates a Retire Prior To value, smaller values sent in
subsequent NEW_CONNECTION_ID frames have no effect. A receiver
[MUST]{.bcp14} ignore any Retire Prior To fields that do not increase
the largest received Retire Prior To
value.[¶](#section-19.15-10){.pilcrow}

An endpoint that receives a NEW_CONNECTION_ID frame with a sequence
number smaller than the Retire Prior To field of a previously received
NEW_CONNECTION_ID frame [MUST]{.bcp14} send a corresponding
RETIRE_CONNECTION_ID frame that retires the newly received connection
ID, unless it has already done so for that sequence
number.[¶](#section-19.15-11){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#frame-retire-connection-id}
::: {#section-19.16 .section}
### [19.16.](#section-19.16){.section-number .selfRef} [RETIRE_CONNECTION_ID Frames](#name-retire_connection_id-frames){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-retire_connection_id-frames}

An endpoint sends a RETIRE_CONNECTION_ID frame (type=0x19) to indicate
that it will no longer use a connection ID that was issued by its peer.
This includes the connection ID provided during the handshake. Sending a
RETIRE_CONNECTION_ID frame also serves as a request to the peer to send
additional connection IDs for future use; see [Section
5.1](#connection-id){.xref}. New connection IDs can be delivered to a
peer using the NEW_CONNECTION_ID frame ([Section
19.15](#frame-new-connection-id){.xref}).[¶](#section-19.16-1){.pilcrow}

Retiring a connection ID invalidates the stateless reset token
associated with that connection ID.[¶](#section-19.16-2){.pilcrow}

RETIRE_CONNECTION_ID frames are formatted as shown in [Figure
40](#fig-retire-connection-id){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.16-3){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-retire_connection_id-frame-}

::: {#fig-retire-connection-id}
::: {#section-19.16-4.1 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
    RETIRE_CONNECTION_ID Frame {
      Type (i) = 0x19,
      Sequence Number (i),
    }
:::

[Figure 40](#figure-40){.selfRef}: [RETIRE_CONNECTION_ID Frame
Format](#name-retire_connection_id-frame-){.selfRef}
:::

RETIRE_CONNECTION_ID frames contain the following
field:[¶](#section-19.16-5){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Sequence Number:

:   The sequence number of the connection ID being retired; see [Section
    5.1.2](#retire-cid){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.16-6.2.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Receipt of a RETIRE_CONNECTION_ID frame containing a sequence number
greater than any previously sent to the peer [MUST]{.bcp14} be treated
as a connection error of type
PROTOCOL_VIOLATION.[¶](#section-19.16-7){.pilcrow}

The sequence number specified in a RETIRE_CONNECTION_ID frame [MUST
NOT]{.bcp14} refer to the Destination Connection ID field of the packet
in which the frame is contained. The peer [MAY]{.bcp14} treat this as a
connection error of type
PROTOCOL_VIOLATION.[¶](#section-19.16-8){.pilcrow}

An endpoint cannot send this frame if it was provided with a zero-length
connection ID by its peer. An endpoint that provides a zero-length
connection ID [MUST]{.bcp14} treat receipt of a RETIRE_CONNECTION_ID
frame as a connection error of type
PROTOCOL_VIOLATION.[¶](#section-19.16-9){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#frame-path-challenge}
::: {#section-19.17 .section}
### [19.17.](#section-19.17){.section-number .selfRef} [PATH_CHALLENGE Frames](#name-path_challenge-frames){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-path_challenge-frames}

Endpoints can use PATH_CHALLENGE frames (type=0x1a) to check
reachability to the peer and for path validation during connection
migration.[¶](#section-19.17-1){.pilcrow}

PATH_CHALLENGE frames are formatted as shown in [Figure
41](#fig-path-challenge){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.17-2){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-path_challenge-frame-format}

::: {#fig-path-challenge}
::: {#section-19.17-3.1 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
    PATH_CHALLENGE Frame {
      Type (i) = 0x1a,
      Data (64),
    }
:::

[Figure 41](#figure-41){.selfRef}: [PATH_CHALLENGE Frame
Format](#name-path_challenge-frame-format){.selfRef}
:::

PATH_CHALLENGE frames contain the following
field:[¶](#section-19.17-4){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Data:

:   This 8-byte field contains arbitrary
    data.[¶](#section-19.17-5.2.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Including 64 bits of entropy in a PATH_CHALLENGE frame ensures that it
is easier to receive the packet than it is to guess the value
correctly.[¶](#section-19.17-6){.pilcrow}

The recipient of this frame [MUST]{.bcp14} generate a PATH_RESPONSE
frame ([Section 19.18](#frame-path-response){.xref}) containing the same
Data value.[¶](#section-19.17-7){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#frame-path-response}
::: {#section-19.18 .section}
### [19.18.](#section-19.18){.section-number .selfRef} [PATH_RESPONSE Frames](#name-path_response-frames){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-path_response-frames}

A PATH_RESPONSE frame (type=0x1b) is sent in response to a
PATH_CHALLENGE frame.[¶](#section-19.18-1){.pilcrow}

PATH_RESPONSE frames are formatted as shown in [Figure
42](#fig-path-response){.xref}. The format of a PATH_RESPONSE frame is
identical to that of the PATH_CHALLENGE frame; see [Section
19.17](#frame-path-challenge){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.18-2){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-path_response-frame-format}

::: {#fig-path-response}
::: {#section-19.18-3.1 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
    PATH_RESPONSE Frame {
      Type (i) = 0x1b,
      Data (64),
    }
:::

[Figure 42](#figure-42){.selfRef}: [PATH_RESPONSE Frame
Format](#name-path_response-frame-format){.selfRef}
:::

If the content of a PATH_RESPONSE frame does not match the content of a
PATH_CHALLENGE frame previously sent by the endpoint, the endpoint
[MAY]{.bcp14} generate a connection error of type
PROTOCOL_VIOLATION.[¶](#section-19.18-4){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#frame-connection-close}
::: {#section-19.19 .section}
### [19.19.](#section-19.19){.section-number .selfRef} [CONNECTION_CLOSE Frames](#name-connection_close-frames){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-connection_close-frames}

An endpoint sends a CONNECTION_CLOSE frame (type=0x1c or 0x1d) to notify
its peer that the connection is being closed. The CONNECTION_CLOSE frame
with a type of 0x1c is used to signal errors at only the QUIC layer, or
the absence of errors (with the NO_ERROR code). The CONNECTION_CLOSE
frame with a type of 0x1d is used to signal an error with the
application that uses QUIC.[¶](#section-19.19-1){.pilcrow}

If there are open streams that have not been explicitly closed, they are
implicitly closed when the connection is
closed.[¶](#section-19.19-2){.pilcrow}

CONNECTION_CLOSE frames are formatted as shown in [Figure
43](#fig-connection-close){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.19-3){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-connection_close-frame-form}

::: {#fig-connection-close}
::: {#section-19.19-4.1 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
    CONNECTION_CLOSE Frame {
      Type (i) = 0x1c..0x1d,
      Error Code (i),
      [Frame Type (i)],
      Reason Phrase Length (i),
      Reason Phrase (..),
    }
:::

[Figure 43](#figure-43){.selfRef}: [CONNECTION_CLOSE Frame
Format](#name-connection_close-frame-form){.selfRef}
:::

CONNECTION_CLOSE frames contain the following
fields:[¶](#section-19.19-5){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Error Code:

:   A variable-length integer that indicates the reason for closing this
    connection. A CONNECTION_CLOSE frame of type 0x1c uses codes from
    the space defined in [Section 20.1](#transport-error-codes){.xref}.
    A CONNECTION_CLOSE frame of type 0x1d uses codes defined by the
    application protocol; see [Section
    20.2](#app-error-codes){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.19-6.2.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Frame Type:

:   A variable-length integer encoding the type of frame that triggered
    the error. A value of 0 (equivalent to the mention of the PADDING
    frame) is used when the frame type is unknown. The
    application-specific variant of CONNECTION_CLOSE (type 0x1d) does
    not include this field.[¶](#section-19.19-6.4.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Reason Phrase Length:

:   A variable-length integer specifying the length of the reason phrase
    in bytes. Because a CONNECTION_CLOSE frame cannot be split between
    packets, any limits on packet size will also limit the space
    available for a reason phrase.[¶](#section-19.19-6.6.1){.pilcrow}

:   

Reason Phrase:

:   Additional diagnostic information for the closure. This can be zero
    length if the sender chooses not to give details beyond the Error
    Code value. This [SHOULD]{.bcp14} be a UTF-8 encoded string
    \[[RFC3629](#RFC3629){.xref}\], though the frame does not carry
    information, such as language tags, that would aid comprehension by
    any entity other than the one that created the
    text.[¶](#section-19.19-6.8.1){.pilcrow}

:   

The application-specific variant of CONNECTION_CLOSE (type 0x1d) can
only be sent using 0-RTT or 1-RTT packets; see [Section
12.5](#frames-and-spaces){.xref}. When an application wishes to abandon
a connection during the handshake, an endpoint can send a
CONNECTION_CLOSE frame (type 0x1c) with an error code of
APPLICATION_ERROR in an Initial or Handshake
packet.[¶](#section-19.19-7){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#frame-handshake-done}
::: {#section-19.20 .section}
### [19.20.](#section-19.20){.section-number .selfRef} [HANDSHAKE_DONE Frames](#name-handshake_done-frames){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-handshake_done-frames}

The server uses a HANDSHAKE_DONE frame (type=0x1e) to signal
confirmation of the handshake to the
client.[¶](#section-19.20-1){.pilcrow}

HANDSHAKE_DONE frames are formatted as shown in [Figure
44](#handshake-done-format){.xref}, which shows that HANDSHAKE_DONE
frames have no content.[¶](#section-19.20-2){.pilcrow}

[]{#name-handshake_done-frame-format}

::: {#handshake-done-format}
::: {#section-19.20-3.1 .artwork .art-text .alignLeft}
    HANDSHAKE_DONE Frame {
      Type (i) = 0x1e,
    }
:::

[Figure 44](#figure-44){.selfRef}: [HANDSHAKE_DONE Frame
Format](#name-handshake_done-frame-format){.selfRef}
:::

A HANDSHAKE_DONE frame can only be sent by the server. Servers [MUST
NOT]{.bcp14} send a HANDSHAKE_DONE frame before completing the
handshake. A server [MUST]{.bcp14} treat receipt of a HANDSHAKE_DONE
frame as a connection error of type
PROTOCOL_VIOLATION.[¶](#section-19.20-4){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#extension-frames}
::: {#section-19.21 .section}
### [19.21.](#section-19.21){.section-number .selfRef} [Extension Frames](#name-extension-frames){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-extension-frames}

QUIC frames do not use a self-describing encoding. An endpoint therefore
needs to understand the syntax of all frames before it can successfully
process a packet. This allows for efficient encoding of frames, but it
means that an endpoint cannot send a frame of a type that is unknown to
its peer.[¶](#section-19.21-1){.pilcrow}

An extension to QUIC that wishes to use a new type of frame
[MUST]{.bcp14} first ensure that a peer is able to understand the frame.
An endpoint can use a transport parameter to signal its willingness to
receive extension frame types. One transport parameter can indicate
support for one or more extension frame
types.[¶](#section-19.21-2){.pilcrow}

Extensions that modify or replace core protocol functionality (including
frame types) will be difficult to combine with other extensions that
modify or replace the same functionality unless the behavior of the
combination is explicitly defined. Such extensions [SHOULD]{.bcp14}
define their interaction with previously defined extensions modifying
the same protocol components.[¶](#section-19.21-3){.pilcrow}

Extension frames [MUST]{.bcp14} be congestion controlled and
[MUST]{.bcp14} cause an ACK frame to be sent. The exception is extension
frames that replace or supplement the ACK frame. Extension frames are
not included in flow control unless specified in the
extension.[¶](#section-19.21-4){.pilcrow}

An IANA registry is used to manage the assignment of frame types; see
[Section 22.4](#iana-frames){.xref}.[¶](#section-19.21-5){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
:::
:::

::: {#error-codes}
::: {#section-20 .section}
## [20.](#section-20){.section-number .selfRef} [Error Codes](#name-error-codes){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-error-codes}

QUIC transport error codes and application error codes are 62-bit
unsigned integers.[¶](#section-20-1){.pilcrow}

::: {#transport-error-codes}
::: {#section-20.1 .section}
### [20.1.](#section-20.1){.section-number .selfRef} [Transport Error Codes](#name-transport-error-codes){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-transport-error-codes}

This section lists the defined QUIC transport error codes that can be
used in a CONNECTION_CLOSE frame with a type of 0x1c. These errors apply
to the entire connection.[¶](#section-20.1-1){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

NO_ERROR (0x00):

:   An endpoint uses this with CONNECTION_CLOSE to signal that the
    connection is being closed abruptly in the absence of any
    error.[¶](#section-20.1-2.2.1){.pilcrow}

:   

INTERNAL_ERROR (0x01):

:   The endpoint encountered an internal error and cannot continue with
    the connection.[¶](#section-20.1-2.4.1){.pilcrow}

:   

CONNECTION_REFUSED (0x02):

:   The server refused to accept a new
    connection.[¶](#section-20.1-2.6.1){.pilcrow}

:   

FLOW_CONTROL_ERROR (0x03):

:   An endpoint received more data than it permitted in its advertised
    data limits; see [Section
    4](#flow-control){.xref}.[¶](#section-20.1-2.8.1){.pilcrow}

:   

STREAM_LIMIT_ERROR (0x04):

:   An endpoint received a frame for a stream identifier that exceeded
    its advertised stream limit for the corresponding stream
    type.[¶](#section-20.1-2.10.1){.pilcrow}

:   

STREAM_STATE_ERROR (0x05):

:   An endpoint received a frame for a stream that was not in a state
    that permitted that frame; see [Section
    3](#stream-states){.xref}.[¶](#section-20.1-2.12.1){.pilcrow}

:   

FINAL_SIZE_ERROR (0x06):

:   \(1\) An endpoint received a STREAM frame containing data that
    exceeded the previously established final size, (2) an endpoint
    received a STREAM frame or a RESET_STREAM frame containing a final
    size that was lower than the size of stream data that was already
    received, or (3) an endpoint received a STREAM frame or a
    RESET_STREAM frame containing a different final size to the one
    already established.[¶](#section-20.1-2.14.1){.pilcrow}

:   

FRAME_ENCODING_ERROR (0x07):

:   An endpoint received a frame that was badly formatted \-- for
    instance, a frame of an unknown type or an ACK frame that has more
    acknowledgment ranges than the remainder of the packet could
    carry.[¶](#section-20.1-2.16.1){.pilcrow}

:   

TRANSPORT_PARAMETER_ERROR (0x08):

:   An endpoint received transport parameters that were badly formatted,
    included an invalid value, omitted a mandatory transport parameter,
    included a forbidden transport parameter, or were otherwise in
    error.[¶](#section-20.1-2.18.1){.pilcrow}

:   

CONNECTION_ID_LIMIT_ERROR (0x09):

:   The number of connection IDs provided by the peer exceeds the
    advertised
    active_connection_id_limit.[¶](#section-20.1-2.20.1){.pilcrow}

:   

PROTOCOL_VIOLATION (0x0a):

:   An endpoint detected an error with protocol compliance that was not
    covered by more specific error
    codes.[¶](#section-20.1-2.22.1){.pilcrow}

:   

INVALID_TOKEN (0x0b):

:   A server received a client Initial that contained an invalid Token
    field.[¶](#section-20.1-2.24.1){.pilcrow}

:   

APPLICATION_ERROR (0x0c):

:   The application or application protocol caused the connection to be
    closed.[¶](#section-20.1-2.26.1){.pilcrow}

:   

CRYPTO_BUFFER_EXCEEDED (0x0d):

:   An endpoint has received more data in CRYPTO frames than it can
    buffer.[¶](#section-20.1-2.28.1){.pilcrow}

:   

KEY_UPDATE_ERROR (0x0e):

:   An endpoint detected errors in performing key updates; see [Section
    6](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9001#section-6){.relref} of
    \[[QUIC-TLS](#QUIC-TLS){.xref}\].[¶](#section-20.1-2.30.1){.pilcrow}

:   

AEAD_LIMIT_REACHED (0x0f):

:   An endpoint has reached the confidentiality or integrity limit for
    the AEAD algorithm used by the given
    connection.[¶](#section-20.1-2.32.1){.pilcrow}

:   

NO_VIABLE_PATH (0x10):

:   An endpoint has determined that the network path is incapable of
    supporting QUIC. An endpoint is unlikely to receive a
    CONNECTION_CLOSE frame carrying this code except when the path does
    not support a large enough MTU.[¶](#section-20.1-2.34.1){.pilcrow}

:   

CRYPTO_ERROR (0x0100-0x01ff):

:   The cryptographic handshake failed. A range of 256 values is
    reserved for carrying error codes specific to the cryptographic
    handshake that is used. Codes for errors occurring when TLS is used
    for the cryptographic handshake are described in [Section
    4.8](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9001#section-4.8){.relref} of
    \[[QUIC-TLS](#QUIC-TLS){.xref}\].[¶](#section-20.1-2.36.1){.pilcrow}

:   

See [Section 22.5](#iana-error-codes){.xref} for details on registering
new error codes.[¶](#section-20.1-3){.pilcrow}

In defining these error codes, several principles are applied. Error
conditions that might require specific action on the part of a recipient
are given unique codes. Errors that represent common conditions are
given specific codes. Absent either of these conditions, error codes are
used to identify a general function of the stack, like flow control or
transport parameter handling. Finally, generic errors are provided for
conditions where implementations are unable or unwilling to use more
specific codes.[¶](#section-20.1-4){.pilcrow}
:::
